<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><img width="232" height="43" src="g165451bev2i001.gif" alt="GRAPHIC"></font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">One AAR

1100 N. Wood Dale Road<br>
Wood Dale, IL 60191</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><hr size="1" width="160" noshade color="black" align="left" style="width:120.0pt;"></div>

<p style="font-weight:bold;line-height:14.0pt;margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:0in;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:normal;">NOTICE OF ANNUAL MEETING OF
STOCKHOLDERS<a name="NoticeOfAnnualMeetingOfStockholde_022732"></a><br>
TO BE HELD ON WEDNESDAY, OCTOBER 18, 2006</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Annual Meeting of
Stockholders of AAR CORP. for the year 2006 will be held at AAR CORP.&#146;s
headquarters, One AAR Place, 1100 North Wood Dale Road, Wood Dale, Illinois, on
Wednesday, October&nbsp;18, 2006, at 9:00&nbsp;A.M. (Chicago time). At the
meeting, stockholders will be asked to:</font></p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 20.0pt;text-indent:-20.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">1.</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Elect three Class&nbsp;I
directors to serve until the 2009 Annual Meeting of Stockholders;</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 20.0pt;text-indent:-20.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2.</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Ratify the appointment
of KPMG LLP as the Company&#146;s independent registered public accounting firm for
the fiscal year ending May&nbsp;31, 2007;</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 20.0pt;text-indent:-20.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">3.</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Approve the
performance goals under the AAR CORP. Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;Incentive Goal
Program; and</p>

<p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 12.0pt 20.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-20.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">4.</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Transact
any other business that may properly come before the 2006 Annual Meeting or any
adjournment(s)&nbsp;or postponement(s)&nbsp;of the meeting.</p>

<div>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><img width="177" height="33" src="g165451dev2i001.gif" alt="GRAPHIC"></font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:8.0pt;">One AAR
Place<br>
1100 N. Wood Dale Road<br>
Wood Dale, Illinois 60191</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">PROXY
STATEMENT<a name="ProxyStatement_021031"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:normal;">ANNUAL MEETING OF STOCKHOLDERS<a name="AnnualMeetingOfStockholders_021053"></a><br>
October&nbsp;18, 2006</font></b></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">I. VOTING
INFORMATION<a name="I_VotingInformation_021104"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This
Proxy Statement and the enclosed proxy card were mailed to stockholders on or
about August&nbsp;31, 2006, in connection with the solicitation of proxies by
the Board of Directors of the Company to be used at the 2006 Annual Meeting (&#147;Annual
Meeting&#148;).</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Who is entitled to
vote?<a name="WhoIsEntitledToVote_021112"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">If you are a stockholder of record (i.e., you hold
your shares in your own name rather than through a broker, bank or other
nominee) on August&nbsp;21, 2006, the Company&#146;s record date, you may vote your
shares at the Annual Meeting. If you are a
street-name stockholder (i.e., you hold your shares through a broker, bank or
other nominee), you are considered a &#147;beneficial owner&#148; of the stock. To vote
those shares at the Annual Meeting, you must give voting instructions to your
broker, bank or other intermediary who is the &#147;nominee holder&#148; of your shares. Brokers,
banks and other nominee holders have been asked to obtain voting instructions
from their beneficial owners. Proxies submitted by nominee holders on behalf of
beneficial owners will count toward a quorum and will be voted as instructed by
the nominee holder. You will receive additional instructions from your broker,
bank or other nominee explaining how you may vote your shares held in street
name. A list of registered stockholders entitled to vote will be available at
the Company&#146;s offices, 1100 N. Wood Dale Road, Wood Dale, Illinois, for 10 days
prior to the meeting and at the meeting location during the meeting.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">How do stockholders
vote by proxy or in person?<a name="HowDoStockholdersVoteByProxyOrInP_021113"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">If you owned common stock of the Company (&#147;Common
Stock&#148;) outstanding at the close of business on the record date, August&nbsp;21,
2006, you may vote at the Annual Meeting by completing, signing, dating and
returning your proxy card in the postage-paid, addressed envelope provided, or
you may vote in person at the Annual Meeting. On that date, 36,669,685 shares
of Common Stock were outstanding. You will have one vote on each matter to be
voted on for each share you owned on the record date.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">How do stockholders
vote by telephone or the internet?<a name="HowDoStockholdersVoteByTelephoneO_021114"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">You are encouraged to
vote either by telephone or the internet. This will eliminate the need to sign,
date and return your proxy card. To vote by telephone or the Internet, enter
the control number assigned to you and imprinted on your proxy card
accompanying this Proxy Statement. <font style="letter-spacing:-.1pt;">You can
vote by telephone 24 hours a day, seven days a week and by Internet until
1:00&nbsp;A.M. (central time) until the day of the Annual Meeting. If you vote
by telephone or the Internet, please do not return your proxy card.</font></font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b>To
vote by telephone:</b></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 50.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="1" face="Wingdings" style="font-size:8.0pt;">&#216;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b>using a touch-tone phone, call 1-800-652-VOTE (8683) toll-free and
follow the voice prompts</b></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b>To
vote by Internet:</b></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt 50.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="1" face="Wingdings" style="font-size:8.0pt;">&#216;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font style="font-weight:bold;">Log
onto the Internet website at </font>http://www.computershare.com/expressvote and enter your voter control number on your
proxy card and mark the appropriate boxes to enter voting instructions</b></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">1</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='1',FILE='C:\fc\23615466601_D11189_1334612\16545-1-de-v2.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug 24 15:46 2006' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">How
does a stockholder revoke a proxy?<a name="HowDoesAStockholderRevokeAProxy_021201"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">You may
revoke your vote at any time before your proxy is exercised, but only by (i)&nbsp;voting
in person at the Annual Meeting, (ii)&nbsp;submitting another proxy by
telephone or the Internet, or (iii)&nbsp;delivering a later dated, signed proxy
to the Secretary of the Company.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">How will proxy holders
vote shares?<a name="HowWillProxyHoldersVoteShares_021202"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Proxies will be voted in
accordance with instructions on the proxy. If no instructions are specified,
the proxy will be voted <i>FOR</i> the
election of the nominees for Class&nbsp;I director designated by the Board, <i>FOR</i> the ratification of the appointment of KPMG LLP as the Company&#146;s
independent registered public accounting firm, <i>FOR</i>
the approval of the performance goals under the AAR CORP. Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;Incentive
Goal Program, and upon any other matter that may properly come before the
Annual Meeting in the discretion and best judgment of the named proxy holders. If
any director nominee becomes unavailable for election for any reason prior to
the Annual Meeting vote, the Board may reduce the number of directors to be
elected or substitute another person as nominee, and the named proxy holders
will vote for the substitute nominee.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">How will votes be
counted?<a name="HowWillVotesBeCounted_021207"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">All votes cast in person or by
proxy will be tabulated by the inspectors of election appointed for the Annual
Meeting. A majority of the outstanding shares of Common Stock entitled to vote,
present in person or represented by proxy at the Annual Meeting, will
constitute a quorum. The inspectors of election will treat directions to
withhold authority, abstentions and broker non-votes (i.e., where a nominee
holding shares for a beneficial owner has not received voting instructions from
the beneficial owner with respect to a particular matter and such nominee does
not possess or choose to exercise his discretionary authority with respect to
such matter) as shares that are present for purposes of determining a quorum.
Directions to withhold authority will have no effect on the election of
directors, because directors are elected by a plurality of votes cast.
Abstentions and broker non-votes will be disregarded for purposes of determining
whether a matter has been approved, because they are not considered votes cast.
It is not anticipated that there will be any broker non-votes on the election
of directors since brokers will have discretion to vote on this proposal.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Who is the Company&#146;s
proxy solicitor?<a name="WhoIsTheCompanysProxySolicitor_021208"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has engaged D. F.
King&nbsp;&amp; Co., 48 Wall Street, New York, New York, to assist the Company
in soliciting proxies at a total estimated cost of $9,500, plus reasonable
out-of-pocket expenses. The cost of soliciting proxies will be paid by the
Company. D. F. King&nbsp;&amp; Co. may solicit proxies by mail, telephone,
facsimile, e-mail, or in person. Certain officers, directors and employees of
the Company may also solicit proxies.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">II. CORPORATE
GOVERNANCE INFORMATION<a name="Ii_CorporateGovernanceInformation_021216"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company has an ongoing commitment to good
governance and business practices. We regularly review our policies and
procedures, giving due consideration to developments in the area of corporate
governance. We comply with all applicable Securities and Exchange Commission (&#147;SEC&#148;)
rules&nbsp;and regulations and New York Stock Exchange (&#147;NYSE&#148;) listing rules&nbsp;and
have adopted additional corporate governance practices that we believe are in
the best interests of the Company and the stockholders.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
following information about the Company&#146;s corporate governance practices is
available on the Company&#146;s web site (www.aarcorp.com/investor relations/corporate
governance):</font></p>

Directors applies to all employees, officers and directors of the Company,
including the Chief Executive Officer, the Chief Financial Officer and the
Chief Accounting Officer and Controller. Employees are encouraged to report any
conduct that they believe in good faith to be in violation of the Code of
Business Ethics and Conduct. Amendments to the Code of Business Ethics and
Conduct and any waivers from the Code granted by the Board to directors or
executive officers will be filed with the SEC in accordance with applicable rules&nbsp;and
regulations or will be posted on the Company&#146;s web site.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company maintains an Ethics
Assist Line through a third-party provider to receive confidential complaints,
information, suggestions or recommendations, anonymously or otherwise,
concerning the Company, its officers, directors and employees, policies,
procedures, employment and business practices, accounting or audit matters,
financial reporting or compliance with other Company policies or applicable
regulatory or legal requirements. The Ethics Assist Line is toll-free and
permits callers, at their election, to identify themselves or remain anonymous.
The Ethics Assist Line can be accessed by dialing 1-800-418-6423
(x227) or via e-mail to &#147;confide2sv@securityvoice.com.&#148;</font></p>

relations/insider trading; to view actual Forms 3, 4 or 5, click on the Insider

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">III. SECURITY

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">

<div>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman"><font style="font-size:10.0pt;text-transform:uppercase;">Section</font>&nbsp;16(a)&nbsp;<font style="text-transform:uppercase;">Beneficial Ownership Reporting Compliance</font><a name="Section16abeneficialOwnershipRepo_015443"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Based
solely upon a review of SEC Forms 3, 4 and 5 and upon related written
representations furnished to the Company with respect to its most recent fiscal
year, each person who, at any time during the fiscal year, was a director,
officer or beneficial owner of more than ten percent of the Common Stock of the
Company filed on a timely basis all reports required by Section&nbsp;16(a)&nbsp;of
the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, as amended, during the most recent fiscal
year, except that (i)&nbsp;the sale of 71 shares used to pay taxes on
restricted stock in October,&nbsp;2001 and (ii)&nbsp;the exercise of a stock
option for 3,000 shares and a resulting reload option grant for 1,221 shares,
in August,&nbsp;2005, were inadvertently filed late for Michael J. Sharp on a
Form&nbsp;4 in September,&nbsp;2005.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;page-break-after:auto;text-align:center;"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">IV. BOARD OF DIRECTORS<a name="Iv_BoardOfDirectors_015454"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Restated Certificate of
Incorporation and By-Laws of the Company provide that the Board shall consist
of between three and fifteen directors, with the exact number of directors to
be set from time to time by the Board. The number of directors is presently set
at nine. The members of the Board are divided into three classes:&#160; Class&nbsp;I (three directors), Class&nbsp;II
(three directors) and Class&nbsp;III (three directors). One class is elected
each year for a three-year term.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A majority of the members of the
Board of Directors must be independent directors under the criteria established
by the Board and under applicable NYSE rules. The Nominating and Governance
Committee and the Board of Directors review each director annually and make a
determination concerning independence after consideration of all known facts
and circumstances. As permitted by the NYSE rules, the Board has established
categorical standards to assist it in determining director independence. The
Company&#146;s &#147;Categorical Standards and Policy for Determining Director
Independence&#148; include all of the elements of the SEC rules&nbsp;and the NYSE
company listing rules&nbsp;with respect to director independence, as well as
those of the Company, and are attached as <i>Appendix 1</i> to
this Proxy Statement. Based on these categorical standards, the Board, at its
meeting in July,&nbsp;2006, considered whether any director had a material
relationship with the Company that would impair the director&#146;s independence. Based
on its review of all relevant facts and information available and the
recommendations of the Nominating and Governance Committee, the Board
affirmatively determined that no director has a material relationship with the
Company and, accordingly, each director is an independent director, except for
David P. Storch due to his status as Chairman of the Board, President and Chief
Executive Officer of the Company. Under the NYSE rules, a director employed by
the Company cannot be deemed to be an independent director.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Independent directors of the
Board meet in executive session without management as part of each regular
session and otherwise when circumstances deem it advisable or necessary. The
Chairman of the Nominating and Governance Committee presides at the executive
session of independent directors.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Stockholders may communicate
with the Board, independent directors as a group, or any individual director or
Committee Chairman by mail addressed to:&#160;
AAR CORP., Attention:&#160; Independent
Directors, or the name of the individual director, c/o Corporate Secretary, AAR
CORP., 1100 N. Wood Dale Road, Wood Dale, Illinois 60191.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">All members of the Company&#146;s
Board of Directors attended the Company&#146;s 2005 Annual Meeting of Stockholders.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During
the fiscal year ended May&nbsp;31, 2006 (&#147;Fiscal 2006&#148;), the Board held four
meetings. Each incumbent director attended at least 90% of the aggregate
meetings of the Board and of the committees on which they served during Fiscal
2006.</font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">6</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">BOARD COMMITTEES<a name="BoardCommittees_015459"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Board has an Audit Committee, a Compensation Committee, a Nominating and
Governance Committee, and an Executive Committee.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Audit
Committee<a name="AuditCommittee_015505"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Audit Committee is comprised entirely of
independent directors qualified to serve on the Audit Committee under
applicable SEC regulations, NYSE rules&nbsp;and the Company&#146;s Categorical
Standards and Policy for Determining Director Independence. Its members are
James E. Goodwin (Chairman), James G. Brocksmith,&nbsp;Jr., Marc J. Walfish,
and Ronald B. Woodard. The Board of Directors has determined that each member
of the Audit Committee is an &#147;audit committee financial expert,&#148; within the
meaning of applicable SEC rules. In addition, the Board of Directors has
determined that simultaneous service by Mr.&nbsp;Brocksmith on the Audit
Committee of more than three public companies does not impair his ability to
effectively serve on the Company&#146;s Audit Committee.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Audit Committee
acts pursuant to its written charter adopted by the Board of Directors. The
charter was last reviewed and approved by the Audit Committee and the Board of
Directors at their July,&nbsp;2006 meetings. The full text of the Audit
Committee charter appears on the Company&#146;s web site. The Audit Committee
Charter is also set forth in Appendix&nbsp;2 to this Proxy Statement and is available
in print to any stockholder upon written request to the Corporate Secretary at
the Company&#146;s address listed on the first page&nbsp;of this Proxy Statement. The
Audit Committee performs the functions described in its charter and, among
other things:</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>approves
and engages the independent registered public accounting firm who audits the
Company&#146;s consolidated financial statements;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>pre-approves
all non-audit/audit related services furnished by the independent registered
public accounting firm;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>maintains
communication between the Board and the independent registered public
accounting firm;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>monitors
the qualifications, independence and performance of the independent registered
public accounting firm;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>oversees
and reviews the Company&#146;s financial reporting processes and practices;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>oversees
and reviews the quality and adequacy of internal controls over financial
reporting, disclosure controls and the organization and performance of the
Company&#146;s internal audit department;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>reviews
the scope and results of audits; and</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>meets
with the independent registered public accounting firm representatives and
internal audit department representative without members of management present.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Audit Committee held seven
meetings during Fiscal 2006. The Audit Committee Report for the fiscal year
ended May&nbsp;31, 2006 (&#147;Fiscal 2006&#148;) appears on page&nbsp;25.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Compensation
Committee<a name="CompensationCommittee_015511"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Compensation Committee is comprised entirely of independent directors as
defined under applicable NYSE rules&nbsp;and the Company&#146;s Categorical
Standards and Policy for Determining Director Independence. Its members are
James G. Brocksmith,&nbsp;Jr. (Chairman), Michael R. Boyce, Ronald R. Fogleman,
and Ronald B. Woodard. The Compensation Committee performs the functions
described in its written charter. The full text of the Compensation Committee
charter appears on the Company&#146;s web site and is available in print to any
stockholder upon written request to the Corporate Secretary at </font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>fixes the compensation of the Chairman, President and Chief Executive
Officer and together with the full Board evaluates the Chief Executive Officer&#146;s
performance;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>administers the Company&#146;s annual cash incentive and long-term stock

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>recommends director compensation and benefits to the Board for approval;
and</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>oversees administration of certain other employee benefit, director

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Compensation Committee held six meetings during Fiscal 2006. The Compensation
Committee Report for Fiscal 2006 appears on page&nbsp;14.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Nominating
and Governance Committee<a name="NominatingAndGovernanceCommittee_015519"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Nominating and Governance Committee is comprised entirely of independent
directors as defined under applicable NYSE rules&nbsp;and the Company&#146;s
Categorical Standards and Policy for Determining Director Independence. Its
members are Ronald R. Fogleman (Chairman), Michael R. Boyce, James E. Goodwin,
and Marc J. Walfish. The Nominating and Governance Committee is responsible for
both nominating and governance functions as described in its charter. The full
text of the Nominating and Governance Committee charter appears on the Company&#146;s
web site and is available in print to any stockholder upon written request to
the Corporate Secretary at the Company&#146;s address listed on the first page&nbsp;of
this Proxy Statement. The Nominating and Governance Committee performs the
functions described in its charter and, among other things:</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>oversees the composition, structure and evaluation of the Board and its
committees;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>develops and recommends corporate governance guidelines for Board
approval; and</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0in 0in 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>monitors and screens directors for independence and recommends to the
Board qualified candidates for election as directors and to serve on Board
committees.</p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
seeking qualified candidates, the Nominating and Governance Committee obtains
referrals from management, other directors and business and community leaders,
and may retain the services of a consultant to assist in identifying candidates.
The Nominating and Governance Committee seeks candidates that complement the
Board as a whole and who collectively are strong and diverse in knowledge,
skills, experience, and background. When selecting nominees, including those
proposed by stockholders, the Committee looks for candidates who are
independent and have a high level of integrity and professional and personal
ethics and values, as well as demonstrated business acumen, leadership and
policy making experience or special technical skills, irrespective of gender or
ethnicity, as well as other factors the Committee deems appropriate. The
Committee has full discretion in considering its nominations to the Board. The
Company&#146;s Director Nominating Process and Selection Guidelines appear on the
Company&#146;s web site and are available in print to any stockholder upon written
request to the Corporate Secretary at the Company&#146;s address listed on the first
page&nbsp;of this Proxy Statement. The Nominating and Governance Committee will
consider director candidates recommended by stockholders in the same manner as
other candidates. Stockholders may submit a proposed nomination to the
Nominating and Governance Committee for consideration with respect to the
Annual Meeting of Stockholders for the year 2007 by writing to the Secretary,
AAR CORP., One AAR Place, 1100 N. Wood Dale Road, Wood Dale, Illinois 60191. To
be considered, proposed nominations must be received prior to April&nbsp;21,
2007, must state the reasons for the proposed </font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">8</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='8',FILE='C:\fc\23795013515_D10466_1336405\16545-1-di-v2.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug 25 09:50 2006' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">nomination
and contain the full name and address of each proposed nominee, as well as a
brief biographical history setting forth past and present directorships,
employment and occupations, and any other qualifications. Proposed nominations
must also include a statement indicating that the proposed nominees have
consented to being named in the proxy statement and to serve if elected. The
Nominating and Governance Committee held five meetings during Fiscal 2006.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Executive
Committee<a name="ExecutiveCommittee_015525"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Executive Committee is comprised of David P. Storch (Chairman), James E.
Goodwin and Marc J. Walfish. Mr.&nbsp;Goodwin and Mr.&nbsp;Walfish are each
independent directors as defined by applicable NYSE rules&nbsp;and the Company&#146;s
Categorical Standards and Policy for Determining Director Independence. The
Executive Committee acts pursuant to its written charter adopted by the Board
of Directors and is authorized to meet between meetings of the Board of
Directors and exercise certain powers of the Board with respect to urgent
matters or other matters referred to it by the Board for deliberation or
action, subject to limitations imposed by the Committee&#146;s charter, the Board,
applicable law and the Company&#146;s By-Laws. The full text of the Executive
Committee charter appears on the Company&#146;s web site and is available in print
to any stockholder upon written request to the Corporate Secretary at the
Company&#146;s address listed on the first page&nbsp;of this Proxy Statement. The
Executive Committee held one meeting during Fiscal 2006, acting as the Pricing
Committee for the Board in connection with a private placement of debt
securities by the Company.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">DIRECTORS&#146; COMPENSATION<a name="DirectorsCompensation_015527"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Director compensation and
benefits are recommended to the Board of Directors from time to time by the
Compensation Committee for Board approval. Currently, each director who is not
an officer or employee of the Company or any subsidiary (&#147;Eligible Director&#148;)
receives an annual retainer of $35,000, a fee of $2,500 for attendance at each
meeting of the Board or of any Board committee attended in person ($1,250 per
meeting for telephonic Board and Committee meetings), plus reimbursement of
expenses. Each committee chairman receives an additional $5,000 annual retainer.
Each Eligible Director may elect to defer receipt of the annual retainer and
meeting fees pursuant to the Company&#146;s Nonemployee Directors&#146; Deferred
Compensation Plan. Deferred retainer fees are converted into stock units
equivalent to shares of Common Stock, and deferred meeting fees are credited
with interest quarterly based on the 10-year United States Treasury Bond
rate. Distributions of deferred retainer fees under the plan occur in cash or
equivalent value Common Stock, at the participant&#146;s election, and distribution
of deferred meeting fees are made in cash upon termination of service on the
Board and on the happening of certain other events, as specified in the plan.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In addition, each Eligible
Director, upon being elected a director, receives term life insurance coverage
of $200,000, and is eligible to receive discretionary stock option grants and
restricted stock awards from time to time under the AAR CORP. Stock Benefit
Plan, as may be determined by the Compensation Committee. Historically, each
non-employee director received an annual stock option grant that expires ten
years from the date of grant and becomes exercisable in 25% increments on each
anniversary grant date at the closing NYSE price on the date of grant. In
Fiscal 2006, the Compensation Committee determined that each non-employee
director should receive an annual restricted stock award of 2,500 shares
(having a fair market value of approximately $40,000 based on then current NYSE
closing price), vesting pro rata over a three-year period. Consistent with the
foregoing, for Fiscal 2007, the Compensation Committee also approved a 2,500
share restricted stock grant for each non-employee director having a grant date
of July&nbsp;11, 2006. Under the Company&#146;s stock ownership guidelines for
directors, each non-employee director is expected to own a minimum of 10,000
shares of Company Common Stock while serving as a director, with such ownership
to be achieved prior to July&nbsp;15, 2009 or within four (4)&nbsp;years of
becoming a director, whichever is later.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The AAR CORP. Directors&#146;
Retirement Plan was terminated effective April&nbsp;10, 2001. Any non-employee
director who was a director on the Plan&#146;s effective date of termination or a
retired director then </font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">9</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='9',FILE='C:\fc\23795013515_D10466_1336405\16545-1-di-v2.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug 25 09:50 2006' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">receiving benefits under the Plan
will continue to be eligible to receive benefits pursuant to the terms of the Plan
as the Plan was in effect and applicable to such participant on the earlier of
the date of Plan termination or date of retirement. Benefits are paid upon
reaching age 65 and retirement from the Board if such director has completed at
least five years of service as a director. Benefits are paid quarterly in cash
in an amount equal to 25% of the annual retainer payable from time to time to
an active director and are paid for a period equal to the total number of years
of service as a director to a maximum of ten years or until death. Continuing
liabilities under the Plan are unfunded. As of May&nbsp;31, 2006, six former
directors are receiving retirement benefits under the Plan, one former director
is eligible to receive benefits under the Plan upon reaching age 65, and one
current director is eligible to receive benefits under the Plan upon retirement
from the Board.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Directors
who are officers or employees of the Company or any subsidiary receive no additional
compensation for service on the Board or any of its committees.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0in 0in 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">CERTAIN RELATIONSHIPS
AND RELATED TRANSACTIONS<a name="CertainRelationshipsAndRelatedTra_015530"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Mr.&nbsp;Ira A. Eichner, a
former director, Chairman of the Board and founder of the Company who retired
on October&nbsp;19, 2005, provides consulting services to the Company pursuant
to a consulting agreement that expires on October&nbsp;18, 2010, under which he
receives a quarterly consulting fee in the amount of $37,500. During Fiscal
2006, Mr.&nbsp;Eichner received $125,000 in consulting fees. Mr. Eichner is Mr.
Storch&#146;s father-in-law.</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">

<div>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">V. PROPOSAL 1<a name="V_Proposal1_015259"></a><br>
ELECTION OF DIRECTORS</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Board of Directors is presently divided into three
classes, each having three-year terms that expire in successive years. The
Board of Directors has nominated three directors to be elected in Class&nbsp;I
at the Annual Meeting, each to serve a three-year term expiring at the 2009
Annual Meeting or until the individual is succeeded by another qualified
director who has been duly elected.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The nominees for Director in Class&nbsp;I
this year are <b>Michael R. Boyce, James G. Brocksmith,&nbsp;Jr.,
and David P. Storch.</b></font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Information about the nominees
and continuing directors whose terms expire in future years is set forth in Section&nbsp;VI
below beginning on page&nbsp;12.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Each
nominee is currently serving as a director of the Company and has been determined
by the Board to be &#147;independent&#148; within the meaning of NYSE rules, except for Mr.&nbsp;Storch
who, as Chairman of the Board, President and Chief Executive Officer of the
Company, is an inside director. The Board expects each nominee to serve if
elected as a director. Under Delaware law and the Company&#146;s By-Laws, the
nominees for director who individually receive the greatest number of votes
shall be elected directors of the Company.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><b><i><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;font-style:italic;">THE BOARD OF DIRECTORS RECOMMENDS THAT<br>
STOCKHOLDERS VOTE <u>FOR</u> ALL NOMINEES</font></i></b></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">

<div>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-align:center;"><b><font size="3" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:12.0pt;">VII. EXECUTIVE
COMPENSATION AND OTHER INFORMATION<a name="Vii_ExecutiveCompensationAndOther_013930"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">COMPENSATION COMMITTEE&#146;S
REPORT ON EXECUTIVE COMPENSATION<a name="CompensationCommitteesReportOnExe_013807"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">General<a name="General_013807"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company&#146;s executive
compensation program is structured and administered by the Compensation
Committee of the Board of Directors. The Compensation Committee is comprised of
the four individuals listed below, each of whom (i)&nbsp;has been determined by
the Board of Directors to be an independent director of the Company under
applicable NYSE rules&nbsp;and the Company&#146;s Categorical Standards and Policy
for Determining Director Independence, (ii)&nbsp;is a non-employee director for
purposes of Rule&nbsp;16b-3 of the Exchange Act, and (iii)&nbsp;is an
outside director for purposes of Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;of the Internal
Revenue Code.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Committee meets at scheduled
times during the year and reports regularly to the Board on Committee actions
and recommendations. In carrying out its responsibilities and duties, the
Committee has the authority to obtain advice and assistance from outside legal,
compensation or other advisors as the Compensation Committee deems necessary to
carry out its duties with funding from the Company.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The compensation program for
executives is designed to enable the Company to attract, motivate and retain
talented executives capable of achieving strategic business initiatives and
producing outstanding business performance and stockholder value. The Company
strives to provide an aggregate compensation opportunity that is competitive
with prevailing practices, aligns stockholder and executive interests, and
reflects total compensation that is justified by individual experience,
performance and business results. A principal compensation guideline of the
Committee is that there be a strong link between pay and performance both at
the Company level and individual level.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Committee intends that the
executive compensation program should complement the Company&#146;s short-term and
long-term business objectives and focus executives&#146; efforts on fulfilling these
objectives. The program consists of three elements:&#160; (i)&nbsp;base salaries which are generally
set between the median and third quartile salary level of comparable positions
in similar companies, adjusted up or down to reflect individual
responsibilities, performance and other relevant factors; (ii)&nbsp;annual
variable incentive opportunities paid in cash based on individual contribution
and performance; and (iii)&nbsp;long-term incentive opportunities, in the form
of stock options and restricted stock awards.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Total
compensation opportunities for each executive are intended to be competitive
with those offered by other companies competing for talent in the Company&#146;s
employment market. In designing and administering the individual elements of
the executive compensation program for each executive, the Compensation
Committee strives to balance short- and long-term incentive objectives and
employ prudent judgment in establishing base salary levels and performance
criteria, evaluating performance and determining actual incentive payments. To
ensure competitiveness and reasonableness of the Compensation Committee&#146;s
compensation decisions, independent compensation consulting firms are retained
periodically to advise the Compensation Committee in connection with both the
design and implementation of the various elements of the program and the level
of individual executive participation. The Company uses competitive
compensation analyses by independent consultants to ensure that the Chairman of
the Board, President and Chief Executive Officer&#146;s and other executive officers&#146;
base salaries and total compensation opportunities (not actual pay) are at an
appropriate competitive level relative to compensation for such positions at
other companies in the relevant employment market. Generally, as an executive&#146;s
level of responsibility increases, a greater percentage of total compensation
opportunity is based on performance, and the mix of total compensation shifts
toward stock, thereby aligning the long-term interest of senior executives with
those of stockholders.</font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">14</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='14',FILE='C:\fc\237115627772_D10466_1336666\16545-1-do-v2.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug 25 11:56 2006' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Base
Salaries<a name="BaseSalaries_013809"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Base
salary levels of all elected corporate officers, including the Chairman of the
Board, President and Chief Executive Officer, are reviewed annually by the
Compensation Committee and may be adjusted depending upon the executive&#146;s
qualifications, responsibilities, assessed performance contribution, tenure in
the Company and in the position held, and competitive salary considerations
relative to similar positions at other companies competing for talent in the
Company&#146;s employment market. In Fiscal 2006, the Compensation Committee
approved merit increases averaging 3% in the aggregate for all employees,
including the Chairman of the Board, President and Chief Executive Officer, and
other named executive officers, with individual increases based on individual
performance. For Fiscal 2007, the Compensation Committee approved merit
increases averaging 3.5% for all employees effective June&nbsp;1, 2006,
including the Chairman of the Board, President and Chief Executive Officer, and
other named executive officers, with actual salary adjustments based on
individual performance after completion of performance reviews, except that
employees earning less than $75,000 annually may receive an additional amount
equal to .5% of their base salary, for Fiscal 2007 only, in consideration of
the effects of high fuel costs on the cost of living.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Annual
Incentive Opportunities<a name="AnnualIncentiveOpportunities_013810"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Company awarded annual cash
incentives for Fiscal 2006 to the Chairman of the Board, President and Chief
Executive Officer of the Company and certain other executive officers of the
Company based on achievement of specific performance goals approved by the
Compensation Committee pursuant to the Company&#146;s stockholder-approved 162(m)&nbsp;Program.
Pursuant to the Company&#146;s 162(m)&nbsp;Program, the Compensation Committee
establishes specific performance goals intended to meet the requirements of Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;of
the Internal Revenue Code (&#147;IRC&#148;). These goals focus on two categories:&#160; income and balance sheet management. For
Fiscal 2006, the income goal was net income, and the balance sheet management
goals were return on investment capital and debt to capital ratio, as
established by the Compensation Committee. The Chairman of the Board, President
and Chief Executive Officer was eligible to earn up to 150% of his base salary
in Fiscal 2006 pursuant to his employment agreement, while the bonus amounts
for other executive officers of the Company vary depending on their position,
the Company&#146;s performance and the Committee&#146;s assessment of their individual
contributions. For Fiscal 2006, the Committee approved awards for the named
executive officers as shown in the &#147;Bonus&#148; column of the Summary Compensation
Table in accordance with the terms of each executive officer&#146;s respective
incentive plan and achievement of applicable performance goals approved by the
Compensation Committee.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As
discussed below under Proposal 3&nbsp;&#151; &#147;Approval of Performance Goals under
the AAR CORP. Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;Incentive Goal Program,&#148; the Company is
asking stockholders to approve the performance goals under a new Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;program,
which encompasses both annual cash incentive opportunities and
performance-based restricted stock award opportunities beginning in Fiscal
2007.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Long-Term
Incentive Opportunities<a name="LongtermIncentiveOpportunities_013834"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">To reward and retain employees
in a manner that best aligns employees&#146; interests with stockholder interests,
the Company implemented the stockholder-approved AAR CORP. Stock Benefit Plan (&#147;Stock
Benefit Plan&#148;). The long-term incentive program consists of stock options,
employment based restricted stock awards, performance based restricted stock
awards, or any combination thereof, granted under the Stock Benefit Plan, in
the discretion of the Compensation Committee. The Stock Benefit Plan also
provides for the use of stock appreciation units; however, to date, none have
been granted. The specific terms of any stock option or restricted stock grants
are determined by the Compensation Committee prior to the issuance of grants,
subject to the provisions of the Stock Benefit Plan.</font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">15</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='15',FILE='C:\fc\237115627772_D10466_1336666\16545-1-do-v2.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug 25 11:56 2006' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Stock option grants typically
expire ten years from the date of grant or earlier upon termination of
employment, become exercisable at fair market value based on the NYSE closing
stock price on the date of grant in equal increments over a period of three to
five years on successive grant anniversary dates or, in some instances, upon
meeting certain share price performance criteria, and, historically, have been
accompanied by reload features (stock option reload features for all active
employees were voluntarily eliminated in Fiscal 2006). Stock option grant dates
are determined by the Compensation Committee and are as of the date of approval
by the Compensation Committee, or if the grant is in connection with a new hire
or promotion of an employee, the grant date is the date of hire or the
promotion date, as applicable. Typically, stock option grants vest in 20%
increments ratably on the grant date anniversary.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Restricted stock grants are designed,
among other things, to align employee interests with the interests of stockholders
and increase stockholder value and to encourage executives to build their
career with the Company. Restricted stock typically vest over periods of three
to ten years from grant date and may be performance-based with vesting to occur
over periods of one to ten years after being earned. The award recipient
receives dividends, if any, on the restricted shares and also has the right to
vote the restricted shares.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Typically, stock options and
restricted stock are subject to forfeiture if the employee terminates
employment for any reason other than death, retirement or disability or the
Company terminates employment for cause, during the grant cycle.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Generally, when determining
stock option and restricted stock grants, the Committee considers the recipient&#146;s
position and responsibilities in the Company, performance and contributions
made during the preceding year, capabilities and potential for future
contribution to the Company, the number of options and restricted stock shares
previously granted to the recipient and, for senior management (including the
named executive officers), their achievement of the Company&#146;s guidelines for
stock ownership. Under new stock ownership guidelines established in Fiscal
2006, the Chairman of the Board, President and Chief Executive Officer is
expected to own Company stock having a value of at least three times his base
salary, other executive officers are expected to own stock having a value of at
least 75% of their base salary, and directors are expected to own 10,000 shares
of Company stock.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">To
maintain consistency with current trends in stock-based compensation, the
Company has adopted several amendments to its Stock Benefit Plan and made other
changes in recent years:</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>The Company voluntarily eliminated the automatic reload feature in its
stock option grants, effective 2005, with all outstanding option agreements
amended to eliminate reloads effective May&nbsp;1, 2006;</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>In anticipation of the effective date of the option expensing requirement
under SFAS No.&nbsp;123(R), &#147;Share-Based Payment&#148; (&#147;SFAS No. 123(R)&#148;), the
Company accelerated the vesting of all outstanding options to May&nbsp;1, 2006
(as a result of this action, approximately 679,400 employee stock
options that were scheduled to vest in Fiscal 2007, 2008 and 2009 became fully exercisable
effective May 1, 2006);</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>The Company eliminated the evergreen provision under its Stock Benefit
Plan and fixed the number of shares available for awards under the Stock
Benefit Plan at the remaining authorized shares available (3,532,226);</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>The Company moved from annual grants of stock options for executives to
performance restricted stock grants with grants being issued based on
performance over a two-year performance period, including a stock price feature
designed to reward key participants only after stockholders have been rewarded.</p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Performance restricted stock
grants are subject to an extended vesting period to align employee interests
with the interests of stockholders and increase stockholder value and to
encourage </font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">16</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='16',FILE='C:\fc\237115627772_D10466_1336666\16545-1-do-v2.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug 25 11:56 2006' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">executives to build their career
with the Company. For Fiscal 2006, the Company achieved the pre-determined
performance targets and the named executive officers received the performance
restricted stock grants reflected in the Summary Compensation table below. The
number of shares granted to an individual reflects the Committee&#146;s assessment
of the individual&#146;s level of responsibility in the Company and ability to
contribute toward achievement of applicable targets and achievement of
performance goals.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As discussed below under
Proposal 3&nbsp;&#151; &#147;Approval of Performance Goals under the Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;Incentive
Goal Program,&#148; the Company is asking stockholders to approve the performance
goals under a new Section&nbsp;162(m)&nbsp;program, which encompasses annual
cash bonuses and long-term stock incentive opportunities, including performance
restricted stock grants for the two-year performance period ended May&nbsp;31,
2008 and subsequent performance periods as approved by the Compensation
Committee.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In addition, the Compensation
Committee also approved stock option grants to a group of key leadership track
employees, excluding named executive officers of the Company, having a grant
date of June&nbsp;1, 2006, at an exercise price of $23.97, the New York Stock
Exchange closing price for the stock on that date.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Executive Perquisites<a name="ExecutivePerquisites_013845"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In addition to the
Company&#146;s Welfare Plans and contractual benefits for executives discussed
elsewhere, it has been the Company&#146;s historical practice to provide certain
other executive perquisites to senior executives. The Company continues this
practice and offers one or more of the following executive perquisites to named
executive officers, depending on the individual executive&#146;s position, years of
service, level of responsibility and total compensation package:</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Annual vehicle allowance.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Reimbursement of pre-approved professional, club and association fees and
charges.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Reimbursement of travel and related expenses in connection with
participation in meetings of pre-approved not-for-profit educational and
professional organizations.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Third party professional executive financial planning assistance.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Reimbursement of professional tax preparation fees.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Executive annual physical and preventative health program.</p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt 30.0pt;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font>Participation in executive housing relocation program, including home
purchase and reimbursement of relocation expenses.</p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The incremental costs of such
perquisites to the Company are included in the Summary Compensation Table below
in accordance with SEC rules.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Chief
Executive Officer Compensation<a name="ChiefExecutiveOfficerCompensation_013853"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">On July&nbsp;11, 2006, the
Compensation Committee completed a performance review of David P. Storch, the
Chairman of the Board, President and Chief Executive Officer of the Company
with an opportunity for input from each member of the Board of Directors. The
Chairman of the Compensation Committee and Chairman of the Nominating and
Governance Committee then met and discussed the results of the review with Mr.&nbsp;Storch.
Mr.&nbsp;Storch&#146;s base salary for Fiscal 2006 was $717,168. Effective June&nbsp;1,
2006, consistent with that provided to other management employees of the
Company, Mr.&nbsp;Storch received a salary increase of 3.5% to $742,269 annually.
Pursuant to his Employment Agreement, for Fiscal 2006, Mr.&nbsp;Storch earned
an annual incentive cash bonus equal to 145% of his base salary in effect on May&nbsp;31,
2006, or $1,041,051, based on the Company&#146;s performance during the period, </font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">17</font></p> <br><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="center">

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='17',FILE='C:\fc\237115627772_D10466_1336666\16545-1-do-v2.htm',USER='jmsproofassembler',CD='Aug 25 11:56 2006' -->
<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">which exceeded pre-established
earnings per share, return on invested capital and long-term debt to capital
ratio goals.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Mr.&nbsp;Storch received 86,667
shares of restricted stock in Fiscal 2006 pursuant to a 2004 performance
incentive opportunity arrangement as a result of the Company&#146;s stock price
increasing to 150% of the stock price on July&nbsp;22, 2005.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As
described below under &#147;Employment and Other Agreements,&#148; Mr.&nbsp;Storch&#146;s
Amended and Restated Employment Agreement provides, with respect to future
compensation, for (i)&nbsp;an annual base salary of not less than $717,168, (ii)&nbsp;an
annual cash incentive bonus opportunity of up to 150% of his base salary based
upon performance against performance goals established by the Compensation
Committee of the Board of Directors and approved by the full Board, and (iii)&nbsp;a
long-term equity incentive compensation opportunity to receive shares of
restricted stock under the Company&#146;s Stock Benefit Plan equal in value of up to
$3.6 million over each of two, two-year performance periods (June&nbsp;1, 2006&nbsp;-
May&nbsp;31, 2008 and June&nbsp;1, 2008&nbsp;- May&nbsp;31, 2010) based upon
performance against specific performance goals established by the Compensation
Committee of the Board of Directors and approved by the full Board and intended
to qualify under the Company&#146;s 162(m)&nbsp;Incentive Goal Program submitted to
stockholders for approval under Proposal 3 below.</font></p>

<p style="font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Federal
Income Tax Considerations<a name="FederalIncomeTaxConsiderations_013855"></a></font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 6.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">IRC Section 162(m) generally prevents any public
company from claiming a deduction for compensation in excess of $1 million for
the Chief Executive Officer or any of the four highest compensated executive
officers. This deduction limitation, however, does not apply to performance-based
compensation that satisfies certain requirements under&#160; Section 162(m). The Compensation Committee
has determined that it is in the best interests of the Company and its
stockholders to structure compensation of executive officers so that compensation
will not be subject to the deduction limit to the extent that it can reasonably
do so in a manner that provides adequate incentives and allows the Company to
attract and retain qualified executives. However, the Compensation Committee
has previously and may in the future structure compensation arrangements that
under certain circumstances may be subject to the deduction limit. None of the
compensation paid by the Company in Fiscal 2006 was subject to the deduction
limit.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0pt 0pt 12.0pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Compensation Committee
also (i)&nbsp;reviewed and assessed the adequacy of the Compensation Committee
charter and recommended certain changes which were adopted by the Board on July&nbsp;12,
2006, and (ii)&nbsp;conducted a Compensation Committee self-assessment in which
it concluded that the Committee operated effectively in carrying out its
charter responsibilities.</font></p>

<p style="font-family:Times New Roman;font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;margin:0pt 0pt 2.0pt 10.0pt;page-break-after:avoid;text-indent:-10.0pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Compensation Committee<a name="CompensationCommittee_013858"></a><br>
</font></b><font style="font-weight:normal;">James
G. Brocksmith,&nbsp;Jr., Chairman<br>
</font><font style="font-weight:normal;">Michael R. Boyce<br>
Ronald R. Fogleman<br>
Ronald B. Woodard</font></p>


 <p style="font-size:10.0pt;margin:24.0pt 0pt .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font face="Times New Roman">18</font></p>
